```

Howard Brazee wrote in message <36349F40.B295F58E@home.com>...
>
>> >In this context, how would you have the gov't deal with food items like
…[12 more quoted lines elided]…
>river for flooding.

Nope. Governments eliminate or remove "nusance" animals,
implement voluntary and mandatory evacuations, and build dams
and levies to protect people and property from immediate harm,
not to punish nature.

The purpose of punishment is to elicit a change in behaviour but it
should be clear that (a personified) nature will always act or react
with impunity since the "nature" of its behaviour can not be changed.
Furthermore, efforts to control nature sometimes result in other
undesirable behaviour. For example, a river that is prevented from
flooding in a particular area will flood another area or take more
of the river bank with it.
-------------------------------
Rick Smith
e-mail: < ricksmith@aiservices.com >
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Y2k Death March Begins.

_(reply depth: 16)_

- **From:** "Donald Tees" <donald@willmack.com>
- **Date:** 1998-10-22T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<70odmi$qa$1@news.igs.net>`
- **References:** `<70g28j$4ue$1@news.igs.net> <19981019192106.27116.00002964@ng63.aol.com> <362c7af8.85223003@news21.bellglobal.com> <70i0a4$jqm$1@news.igs.net> <RB%W1.425$Se2.633786@news4.mia.bellsouth.net> <70i336$lc8$1@news.igs.net> <slrn72sfao.di.cadams@cadams-ntw.acucorp.com> <362ECD69.4BBB971A@att.net> <70n8qh$240$1@news.igs.net> <UkIX1.1026$Se2.1886209@news4.mia.bellsouth.net> <70nqeo$et9$1@news.igs.net> <boLX1.1980$xx4.1981762@news3.mia.bellsouth.net>`

```

Judson McClendon wrote in message ...

>Perhaps I misunderstood you, but the phrase "start using price (via tax)
>as a control method on supply lines" made me think you were thinking to
>use the high price (via high tax) of legal drugs to curtail use.  If that
>were the case, then the legal price would have to be much higher than
>the current illegal price, giving plenty of room for illegal profit. :-)


That obviously would not work.  Cigarettes here in Ontario are probably
a perfect example.  Several years back, the government whacked the
price way up. (four bucks per pack).  Usage started to decline, and
kept declining.  Then the next government figured that a good thing should
be overdone.  They doubled the price.  Within months, there was a
major industry smuggling cigarettes in from New York State. (a buck
fifty a pack).  Things started getting nasty with guns going off.  The
government was defeated, and the new one dropped the price as
a popularity measure to three bucks a pack. The crime stopped overnight
and usage started to climb. In the next budget, they jumped it back
to four, and usage has started to go down again.

Systems are systems, and the parameters that affect them can
be looked at and manipulated.  The problem is that you have
to accept reality to do it, and most of the decisions are being made
on the basis of emotion and rhetoric.

If pot were sold in government stores at $25.00 per ounce (current
street price is about $280), it would wipe out the criminal element,
and fund every rehab center in north America. Even for the worst
drugs, like crack and heroin, the biggest social problem is not the
physiological effect of the drug on the person, it is the economic
effect of addicts engaging in crime to GET the drug.

One has to ask the question of what is worse, allowing addicts
to endanger their own lives with drugs, or exposing everyone to gun
fights in the streets over control of the drug trade. Drugs, (and
I include alcohol as a drug) as involved in about 85% of all
violent crime. That is not because the drugs cause the violence.
It is the *price* of the drugs that cause the violence.
```

```
Mike, did you ever hear of Al Capone? Or the St. Valentines Day
massacre?  That was over prohibition, and over alcohol. Gang
warfare in the states was INVENTED to control illegal booze. The
violence continues because there are people that think the best way
to solve problems is to grab a ".45" and go out and shoot somebody.

>gangs running the supply of crack.  in my town (macon, ga pop 150,000)
>there are over 1000 gang members in 15 gangs.  want to know their
>biggest fear?  a CITIZEN with a .45 in "condition one".  no gov't law

I live in a city of 1.5 million.  Here, we put citizens that grab .45's and
use them
to shoot people in jail.  We put drug addicts in drug rehabilitation
clinics. In the
twenty years that I have lived here, there have been two murders.  The
deaths
due to crack have been OD's.  I just came back from a walk through the
downtown area.  It is 2:30 in the morning. I walked for an hour, and stopped
and chatted with several street people.  It was quite a pleasant walk, and I
enjoyed it.  Could you do that?

You say "you and me" can solve the drug problem.  Although I have been clean
for four years, I am a crack cocaine addict.  I spent roughly $10,000 last
year
putting two street addicts from my neighbourhood through rehab, and at the
moment have a third staying at my house while waiting for her first
apartment
in fifteen years.  The rent is paid for the first and last month (I
co-signed) and
she moves in on the first.  I enjoy my life, and can go anywhere in this
town,
including covert crack houses, unarmed, with no fear, and be treated with
respect by both the crack addicts and the local narcotics squad.  It sounds
to me like your way does not work as well as mine.

You are quite right in one thing, though, this is getting seriously off
topic, so
this will be my last post in this thread.  If anybody would like to continue
it,
we can do so in private mail, or switch over to one of the empty NG's that

that can be used as private channels.

Donald@willmack.com
Donald Tees, Kitchener, Ontario, Canada.

off to you as an example.  It is a program that keeps track of the number
of days, hours and minutes that an addict has been clean. It will handle
five
addicts.  I wrote it several years back, when I was getting clean myself.
For
now, I am going to bed.

Donald.
```

```
Doug Miller wrote in message <70kdek$1vg_002@news.netdirect.net>...

>Since we're going off-topic already...can anyone think of a single reason
>why the production, distribution, possession, and use of marijuana should
>be regulated differently in any fashion from the production, distribution,
>possession, and use of ethyl alcohol?
>
Sure.  As someone that has spent every Sunday for the last two years
in either a jail or a rehab centre giving counceling, I would suggest that
alcohol should be more tightly controlled because it is more addictive
and more damaging to both the body and the psyche.

As far as danger goes, I would rate alcohol as the most dangerous drug,
heroin second, with crack cocaine in a close tie, regular cocaine third
nicotine fourth, and pot  a rather mild fifth.

I know personally of several cases where pot served as a treatment
for addiction to other drugs, though the conquering of *all* dependencies
is the only really satisfactory end goal.
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Y2k Death March Begins.

_(reply depth: 10)_

- **From:** "Judson McClendon" <judmc123@bellsouth.net>
- **Date:** 1998-10-20T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<Mk2X1.466$Se2.714049@news4.mia.bellsouth.net>`
- **References:** `<70g28j$4ue$1@news.igs.net> <19981019192106.27116.00002964@ng63.aol.com> <362c7af8.85223003@news21.bellglobal.com> <70i0a4$jqm$1@news.igs.net> <RB%W1.425$Se2.633786@news4.mia.bellsouth.net> <70i5qn$ogj$1@oak.prod.itd.earthlink.net>`

```
Jeff Farkas wrote:
>
>Judson McClendon wrote:
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
>in Great Britain it was 17.5%!!! That hurts...

The total tax burden here in the U.S. a bit above 45%, and that is on
total income.  Sales tax in my part of the country is 8%-9%.  I don't
expect to pay less money.  I would be willing to pay more money, if only
the IRS was out of our affairs.  I was audited in 1996 for 1992-1995,
and it was not a nice experience.  I pay taxes honestly, and there was no
problem with that, they never questioned my returns as far as accuracy.
But the process was extremely disruptive and intrusive.  For example,
they went through all my check books, line by line.  If you ever get an
IRS auditor who decides to give you a hard time, they can practically
destroy your life on a whim.  To me it is unthinkable that in a 'free'
society an honest citizen would be subjected to such risk of harm and
violation of their privacy by the government during the normal course of
business.  An honest person should have no reason to fear the government.
But there is hardly a person in the U.S. whose heart wouldn't skip a beat
on learning they were going to be audited by the IRS.  That is tyranny.
```

```
move to a state with an equal or lower tax burden.

I ended up in Texas.  Slightly higher cost of living, but still NO 
income taxes, sales tax a little over 8%, but does NOT include food. 
(Except snack food).
```

```
On Thu, 22 Oct 1998 22:42:24 -0400, Jeff Farkas
<JeffreyFarkas@~nospam~earthlink.net> wrote:
>> >You got that right. All I know is that is sounded very funny to me, sort of
>> >like the "Pet Rock" of the late 90's. :-)
…[11 more quoted lines elided]…
>I am just guessing. What in the world is a Tamagotchi???

It was the first of the "virtual pets". Basically you have a simulated creature
that you must feed by pressing a button, play with by pressing other buttons
and so forth. If you don't feed it, it will die. If you don't play with it, it
will die. For inexplicable reasons, some people get very attached to them (It
sounds way too much like admining an NT farm to get me interested). Some people
have driven off the road or into things because their tamagotchi started to
beep about needing food or attention. They start playing with it and forget
what they're doing...
```

```
On Thu, 22 Oct 1998 22:42:24 -0400, Jeff Farkas
<JeffreyFarkas@~nospam~earthlink.net> enlightened us:

>
>
…[21 more quoted lines elided]…
>

Tamagotchi is a small computer game that simulates caring for a pet or
a baby.  I believe the first one was a chicken.  What happens is, the
pet will require feeding, nurturing and sleeping.  It will make
obnoxious sounds if these things are not done.  The user provides
feeding etc. by pressing buttons on the device which is just a little
larger than a digital watch.  If you don't take care of your pet, it
will die!

These things were a big fad with the kids last year and became quite a
nusiance for teachers (sounds going off in the middle of class etc.)
that many schools band them.

They started in Japan, but have spread to just about everywhere.  I
haven't heard or seen much about them lately, so maybe the fad is
dying out.

Cheers,


>
>Jeff
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
>

         (o o)
-oOO--(_)--OOo-
Cats know how we feel. They don't give a damn, but they know.
 Steve
```

```
On Wed, 21 Oct 1998 22:53:04 -0400, Jeff Farkas
<JeffreyFarkas@~nospam~earthlink.net> wrote:
>>  want to know where your fed tax dollars go?
>
>How about the DOD study of caffienated chewing gum!!!

I seem to recall a couple of Dave Barry columns, one about the military buying
$400K *combat* Fax Machines[1] and another about how some government agency was
storing dead radioactive beagles in a freezer. 

Of course, I always enjoyed the way the city council handled a lean year in a
place I used to live: while closing libraries and cutting back office hours and
services everywhere, they paid an "artist" a couple hundred grand to build a
statue by the pier. Said statue was a piece of pipe with a bend in it, placed
in the surf so water could shoot out the top. Of course, the council was
apparently unaware that water in the ocean contains salt, which promptly
started corroding said work of "art". 


[1] Designed to handle the rigors of combat conditions. Left unanswered, of
course, are the questions such as: what would you want to fax in combat or why
night buy 20 $200 civilian fax machines and replace as needed...
```

- **References:** `<70g28j$4ue$1@news.igs.net> <19981019192106.27116.00002964@ng63.aol.com> <362c7af8.85223003@news21.bellglobal.com> <70i0a4$jqm$1@news.igs.net> <RB%W1.425$Se2.633786@news4.mia.bellsouth.net> <70i5qn$ogj$1@oak.prod.itd.earthlink.net>`

```
Jeff Farkas <JeffreyFarkas@~nospam~earthlink.net> wrote:

>
>
…[9 more quoted lines elided]…
>in Great Britain it was 17.5%!!! That hurts...

and we still pay income tax too..

>To our friends in the UK please correct me if I am wrong.
>Also, what is used to determine when to apply VAT??

The rules are arcane in the extreme,  and somewhat arbitrary..  A
couple of examples..

Plain biscuits are considered "food" and thus have a VAT rate of zero
percent.  Chocolate biscuits are "luxuries" and are thus taxed at the
standard rate of 17.5%.  A box of mixed biscuits,  should in theory,
always be open by the retailer who should then count the number of
each type of biscuit and pro-rata the tax accordingly..  :-)

There is a type of "cattle nut" which is normally fed to cattle,  and
as such carries no VAT as it is "food for cattle" and is covered by
the "food" rules..  These nuts can also be fed to horses,  which are
considered a "luxury" sporting item,  and thus subject to VAT..  Thus
one item can be either zero rated or standard rated depending upon its
final use..

Other areas are somewhat more complex..  :-)
```

```
> >To our friends in the UK please correct me if I am wrong.
> >Also, what is used to determine when to apply VAT??
…[15 more quoted lines elided]…
> final use..

VATs scare me.

In the states though we can sometimes be taxed differently for the same
object.  In some states you may be asked whether you are going to use
some liquid as a mouthwash or a gargol.  The first is a cosmetic, and
the latter is a medicine...

But I really don't want to approach finding which taxes are fair - a
better appoach is to limit government spending.  Say, we prohibit them
from increasing spending in any department (without 2/3 war or emergency
type vote) if the previous year the government spent more than 15% of
the GDG.  With this approach, there is little incentive to finding more
ways to sneak our money from us (hurting our economy).  They may choose
to tweak where the money comes from - but not with the goal of having
more money to spend.
```
